Production</li><li>Elastic version - 6.4 (later versions available but not mentioned as supported <a class="external-link" href="https://moodle.org/plugins/search_elastic" rel="nofollow">https://moodle.org/plugins/search_elastic</a>)</li></ol></li><li>Step 2 - Configure domain<ol><li>Elastic domain name - ucl-global-search</li><li>Availability zones - 3AZ</li><li>Instance type - <span>t3.medium</span></li><li>nodes - 3</li><li>Data nodes storage type - EBS</li><li>EBS volume type - SSD</li><li>EBS storage size per node - 20GB</li></ol></li><li>Step 3 - Configure access and security<ol><li>Network configuration - VPC</li><li>Access policy - IAM</li><li>Encryption - HTTPS, node to node encryption, enable encryption at <h1>Myportfolio</h1>

<p>Average portfolio size:<br />
number of profiles now:<br />
expected number by Summer 2010:<br />
expected number by Summer 2011:</p>21160443611994077<p>Licia Capra &lt;l.capra@cs.ucl.ac.uk&gt;<br />
Rachel Cooper &lt;rachel.f.cooper@ucl.ac.uk&gt;<br />
Pete Roberts &lt;p.roberts@ucl.ac.uk&gt;</p>

<h4>What are ISD's regulations/approval process for new plugins?</h4>

<p>A request for new functionality or a plugin is sent to ltss@ucl.ac.uk (Learning Technology Support Service). LTSS will evaluate the suitably of the plugin/request. If it is thought to be suitable for UCL Moodle LTSS will ask Apps Dev to install it on our development instance of Moodle. They will then test the plugin. If it looks good it will then be installed on our pre-production server where we may ask the user to test it, and also test the rest of Moodle to check that it has not had an adverse effect on exiting Moodle functionality. All being well we will schedule a date for it to be installed on our live server, advertising an outage to users if necessary. We try to only make changes to the production Moodle servers outside of term time.</p>

<h4>How long does this process take?</h4>

<p>Depends on the urgency of the plugin/functionality and the other commitments/projects that the LTSS and Apps Dew teams are involved in eg if it is a security fix it will be tested and pushed to production Moodle ASAP, if it added functionality only requested by one user that other users are unlikely to use we may wait until the end of term.</p>

<h4>How has UCL's Moodle installation been edited/hacked versus the generic Moodle install?</h4>

<p>We have three or four hacks to the main Moodle code - plus about the same for third party plugins (but the latter tend to stay the same during upgrades). The code is held in a Subversion repository and it's quite easy to see what's changed with new releases.</p>

<p>We also have a selection of UCL themes - including some new ones in the pipleline.</p>

<h4>Can we further hack the moodle installation to work with our app if needed?</h4>

<p>Hacks to UCL Moodle are for anything considered business-critical by LTSS or Apps Dev. We have been reducing the number of hacks carried out to simplify upgrading.<br />
Any requests for changes to the Moodle service and it's functionality should be sent to ltss@ucl.ac.uk where they will be evaluated and tested as described above.</p>

<h4>What is ISD's upgrade policy for Moodle? (How often is Moodle upgraded?)</h4>

<p>Something of a balancing act - changes to the user interface are rarely popular, but on the other hand we are keen to roll out new features and make the system more secure and stable.</p>

<p>As upgrades are released for Moodle we test and then install them, we currently run the latest release of Moodle (version 1.9.6). If a new version comes out which includes serious security patches we will try to get it pushed to production Moodle ASAP, otherwise we will wait for a convenient time, eg outside of term time, to upgrade to reduce the time that Moodle is unavailable to users. On rare occasions we will patch individual library files such as with the recent SQL injection exploit (after testing).
<br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<h4>What are the UCL data security regulations?</h4>

<p>See the Computer Security Team website at <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/isd/common/cst">http://www.ucl.ac.uk/isd/common/cst</a></p>

<h4>How can ISD provide test environment for our app</h4>

<p>If LTSS feel that it is an appropriate tool for UCL Moodle we can install it on our development and then pre-production servers for testing. While you are testing/developing your app you may want to install your own Moodle instance. If you require any additional settings such as PHP extensions to be enabled etc please keep us informed.</p>

<h4>Are Apple iPhone/iPod touches supported by Roamnet or Eduroam</h4>

<p>There is no compatible VPN client for iPhone/iPod and Roamnet, but these do work with Eduroam</p>

<p>See <a class="external-link" href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/isd/students/wireless" rel="nofollow">http://www.ucl.ac.uk/isd/students/wireless</a> or email roamnet-support@ucl.ac.uk for more information.</p>


<h4>How open is UCL with using new protocol (if not already in use) like SOAP (Simple Object Access Protocol)</h4>

<p>Assuming there is a business case for a new technology - it would need to be ok'd by ISD's Enterprise Architect.<br />
See <a class="external-link" href="http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/InfoSysISDTechStds/ISD+Technical+Standards" rel="nofollow">http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/InfoSysISDTechStds/ISD+Technical+Standards</a></p>

<p>Again, these would be subject to evaluation/testing by LTSS.</p>

<h4>Does ISD know about other universities Moodle system?</h4>

<p>We are on several mailing lists eg moodle-uk@jiscmail.ac.uk where institutions (schools, colleges universities) can post/reply to queries. We attended the UK MoodleMoot conference (<a href="http://moodlemoot.org/">http://moodlemoot.org/</a>) last Easter where we made contact with other places running Moodle - Bath, LSE for example. We are keen to make links with other institutions. </p>21196136111994755<h1>Moodle 1.9.7 testing</h1>

21196208213009671<h1>Restoring a course that has been accidentally deleted</h1>

<p>A Moodle course has two main components:</p>
<ul>
	<li>database entries (spanning numerous tables) in the moodle database on moodledb</li>
	<li>physical files (contained in the moodledata folder for that course - residing on moodle-c /data/moodle)</li>
</ul>


<p>When a course is deleted - both of the above are deleted. Restoring a course is therefore slightly fiddly - it involves restoring a snapshot of Moodle with the course in it - and then using Moodle admin functions to backup the course so it can be moved across back to the live server.</p>

<p>Example - course id 1346 has been deleted in error. Follow these steps:</p>
<ol>
	<li>ask the is-storage team to retrieve the moodledata folder for that course from the appropriate date (most recent probably)</li>
	<li>retrieve the most recent moodle database (probably the night before the course was deleted) using scandump - <a href="http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/ISDMySQL/Running+the+MySQL+service">see Jack's notes here</a></li>
	<li>on a test instance of moodle (either your local machine or on wasdev) - create a new instance of moodle using the database snapshot - get the restored moodledata folder and put it in place</li>
	<li>go into the course and do a course backup - select everything</li>
	<li>this will create a moodle backup zip file</li>
	<li>note that LTSS are very familiar with the backup and restore process and can probably take over at this point - otherwise - you can restore this zip file as a test on wasdev or pp - when you're happy with the process - restore it to live UCL Moodle.</li>
</ol>


<h4>Items to note</h4>

<p>The restored course will have a different ID number. Also the Moodle backup and restore doesn't necessarily include all modules - so for example the flv player plugin - any items there will need setting up again.</p>

<p>It is possible there may have been a manual course backup taken, in which case it will be in the restored moodledata folder - check with the user to see if this is appropriate to restore from - if so it would save having to restore the database snapshot.</p>



<p><br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<p>See also <a href="http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/ISMoodle/Restoring+a+snap+shot+of+Moodle+from+Backup">http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/ISMoodle/Restoring+a+snap+shot+of+Moodle+from+Backup</a></p>21297694213566273<p>Log rotation is now enabled on the Moodle servers - so we can take a look at the access logs and carry out some simple analysis on them in terms of server traffic. It isn't clear at this stage how much of this activity is background noise (bots / spiders etc). The access logs don't seem to contain suffficient detail (user agent etc).</p>

<p>example log entry:<br />
128.40.222.163 - - <ac:link><ri:page ri:content-title="10:20:38 +0000" ri:space-key="10/Dec/2009" /></ac:link> &quot;GET /mod/scorm/view.php?id=249595 HTTP/1.1&quot; 200 14861</p>

<h1>Capacity planning</h1>

<p>Likely scenarios to consider:</p>
<ol>
	<li>New people at UCL start using Moodle</li>
	<li>Existing Moodle users start using Moodle more</li>
	<li>Courses get bigger, more flash, PPTs, audio, video etc</li>
	<li>Growth in new Moodle users from outside UCL - short courses / CPD</li>
</ol>


<p>Technically, there are three areas to consider</p>
<ol>
	<li>Moodle database</li>
	<li>application servers</li>
	<li>filestore for Moodle data.</li>
</ol>


<p>And we need to look at:</p>
<ol>
	<li>performance</li>
	<li>resilience</li>
	<li>disk space</li>
</ol>


<h4>Usage levels and points to note</h4>

<p>There are roughly 21,000 students (but only 18,000 are on taught programmes) and 4000 academic staff at UCL - so around 22,000 likely users of Moodle (26000 if we include all research students but this isn't likely in foreseeable future). We're approaching 19,000 unique users per month - so that would imply a fair proportion of people are logging in. However - they are not logging in that often. The graph below shows that the majority of people login a fairly low number of times across the month - admittedly this was December - but the service usage figures from LTSS across the year show a similar discrepancy between unique logins and the total number of logins - perhaps indicating that a small number of courses are heavy users of Moodle.</p>

<p>&nbsp; <ac:image ac:thumbnail="true"><ri:attachment ri:filename="moodle-logins.png" /></ac:image></p>

<p>Looking at the number of live courses - it would appear we are roughly 45% of the way towards having all courses with a presence in Moodle. However - a large number of the live courses are test or training courses.</p>

<p>Moodle currently contains a number of non-live courses from previous years. It is therefore tricky to calculate how much disk space is in use by live courses.</p>

<p>It seems likely that the number of Moodle users will not increase significantly as most are already using it. It is likely that usage by existing users will increase - but slowly.</p>

<h4>Database</h4>

<p>Moodle is currently performing well - the new database servers showed a distinct performance improvement over the old ones (<a href="http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/ISMoodle/UCL+Moodle+load+testing">see the load test figures</a>). We have also disabled Moodle backups.</p>

<p>However we may lose that advantage by hosting other databases on the Moodle db servers - Opinio and Mahara. Not sure what load they will place on the server. Opinio is around 1Gb or so - Mahara an unknown quantity.</p>

<p>In terms of disk space on the Moodle database server, we should be ok for some time despite Nagios warnings recently,&nbsp;</p>
<ul>
	<li>the largest tables in Moodle are mdl_log&nbsp; - this is big and will get bigger as usage goes up but is truncated after 365 days and pruned monthly by apps dev</li>
	<li>second largest is mdl_backup_log&nbsp; - this is no longer used - will in fact get gradually deleted over the year</li>
	<li>the remaining 270-odd tables are small in comparison - in total they occupy 40% of the disk space used by the Moodle database - put another way - the two log tables hog 60% of the disk space!</li>
</ul>


<p>A sits integration database could potentially get sizeable and impact on performance (at least overnight) - need to get figures from Taliesin - but unlikely to be much bigger than the Moodle db.</p>

<h4>Application servers</h4>

<p>Moodle servers - these haven't complained via Nagios since we turned off the backups. At present it's a bit one-sided as moodle c runs the CRON job and also hosts the moodledata folder. Despite that it seems ok. We may in future find that moving C out of the farm will allow it to run the CRON job / SITS stuff if it proves to slow the server down.</p>

<p>Advice on Moodle.org seems to be the web server itself isn't the bottleneck. We have more hardware than Bath in this respect.
<br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<h4>Filestore for Moodledata</h4>

<p>Disk space for Moodledata and its availability/resilience is likely to be the main issue as Moodle usage increases.</p>

<p>Moodledata is currently hosted on Moodle C with a CRON job to RSYNC a copy hourly to A and B.</p>

<p>There are three main problems with this:</p>
<ul>
	<li>lack of disk space - we are running out slowly - 220Gb remaining</li>
	<li>it's on Moodle C - ideally would be a separate box</li>
	<li>lack of resilience - if Moodle C fails - we potentially lose up to an hours worth of data&nbsp;&nbsp;</li>
</ul>


<p>A better solution would be to have a separate filestore for Moodle data - split across two locations for resilience - and expandable so we can add extra capacity painlessly.</p>

<p>In terms of disk space - regardless of how we implement the archiving of old courses - in future we will need to retain everything in the moodle data folder for a course for the length of the particular degree programme to allow students to revisit previous work. This time span varies depending on the course from three to seven years.</p>

<p>If we say half the courses are currently online and that is taking approximately 250gb - then we would need at least 500gb per year.&nbsp;</p>

<p>5TB ought to keep us going for a few years.</p>

<p>It's worth noting that the OLM file service and Moodle 2 may have an impact on this - but it seems inevitable that we will always need more disk space than we estimate for. For example - the ECDL scorm modules are around 600Mb per course.</p>

<h4>Recommendations<ac:emoticon ac:name="question" /></h4>

<ul>
	<li>address the moodledata issue - a separate, expandable filestore will improve resilience and ease the load on the existing servers</li>
	<li>look at a separate db server for Mahara if it takes off</li>
</ul>

<p>In the central MySQL Config file:<br />

<blockquote>
<p><strong>Steve Ford (Systems) advises:</strong><br />
This is a necessary change for the UCL Advances project, but my understanding is that it is currently only preventing three character searches for videos.  The problem is that &quot;UCL&quot; is three characters, but in reality the severity might only be mild.  What I am meaning is that it probably isn't an urgent change and could be delayed if there is significant difficulty in rebuilding the indexes or getting an outage window.<br />
Since it is only three character searching having problems, the rest of the website should probably still work well.</p></blockquote>

Publicity to users?</p>

<h1><strong>PHP on the central web servers</strong></h1>


<h4>PHP Standards group</h4>

<p><a class="external-link" href="http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/MSDUCLPHP/Home" rel="nofollow">http://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/MSDUCLPHP/Home</a></p>

<h4>wwwa-c/d/e/f</h4>

<p>latest on these servers</p>

<p>taking pdo of -d</p>

<p>safe mode</p>


<h4>requests for PHP extensions on central web servers</h4>


<p><a href="http://uk3.php.net/manual/en/xsl.setup.php">http://uk3.php.net/manual/en/xsl.setup.php</a><br />
This extension uses libxslt which can be found at <a href="http://xmlsoft.org/XSLT/">http://xmlsoft.org/XSLT/</a>. libxslt version 1.1.0 or greater is required.<br />
PHP 5 includes the XSL extension by default and can be enabled by  adding the argument --with-xsl\[=DIR]&nbsp; to your configure line. DIR is  the libxslt installation directory.</p>

<p><a href="http://www.php.net/manual/en/pdf.installation.php">http://www.php.net/manual/en/pdf.installation.php</a><br />
This PECL extension is not bundled with PHP<br />
The notes from other users advise using open source &quot;FPDF&quot; instead as  it has better functionality. FPDF requires no extension (except zlib  to activate compression and GD for GIF support)<br />
<a href="http://www.fpdf.org">http://www.fpdf.org</a></p>

21460083014642585<h1>Sits integration overview - the old method (still in use June 2011)</h1>

<p>The process was as follows:</p>
<ul>
	<li>at around 2am - an export of Portico was created in nfs/rcs/sysman/cso/sits/</li>
	<li>a further CRON job ran the SITSfilter c program to read this in and output it using the modulelist.txt mappings</li>
	<li>written out to /sits_filtered.xml</li>
	<li>IMS enterprise enrolment reads it in to Moodle\</li>
	<li>see <a href="https://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/ISMoodle/user+account+import">https://wiki.ucl.ac.uk/display/ISMoodle/user+account+import</a></li>
</ul>


<h1>Sits integration overview - the new method</h1>

<p>The process is / will be as follows:</p>
<ul>
	<li>at around 2am - an export of Portico is created in nfs/rcs/sysman/cso/sits/</li>
	<li>a CRON job at 2.20am will copy this to /home.local/ccspmdl</li>
	<li>a further CRON job at 2.35am will then run the SITSfilter script to read this in and store it</li>
	<li>a filtered version is then written out to /sits_output.xml</li>
	<li>IMS enterprise enrolment reads it in to Moodle</li>
</ul>


<h1>Differences between the new and old</h1>

<ul>
	<li>the output file name is different (which means we can switch between them in the IMS enterprise enrolment in Moodle if necessary)</li>
	<li>all module information was thrown out previously - which meant we couldn't create courses - new system can create courses if we decide to enable it in Moodle</li>
	<li>the SITS information is stored as a snapshot in a database - students, modules, membership - allows reporting / querying</li>
	<li>the module list txt file has been replaced by database tables</li>
	<li>previously there was no error checking in the modulelist.txt file - there is now</li>
	<li>sitsfilter checks against Moodle before adding to the outputted XML file - so should be smaller / lighter</li>
</ul>


<h1>Constraints</h1>

<ul>
	<li>idnumber field in Moodle courses MUST be unique (in fact won't always work in old method if not)!</li>
	<li>idnumber should be less than 30 characters and contain only alphanumeric chars and underscores or dashes - no ampersands / colons / slashes etc.</li>
	<li>auto populating tutor info will be a phase 2 thing</li>
</ul>


<h1>Steps needed in July 2011 (nb change freeze 16 Sept)</h1>


<ul>
	<li>note - the big switchover to 11/12 happens on 1 AUG</li>
	<li>---</li>
	<li>run the duplicate idnumber report and remove dupe ids from Moodle (LTSS doing this)</li>
	<li>remove the erroneous entries from modulelist.txt (Pete has done this)</li>
	<li>get the categories in Moodle to match those in Portico (Jess has done this)</li>
</ul>


<p><strong>On DEV</strong></p>

<ul>
	<li>Pete to set up a 'data cleaned' version of the SITS filter on the dev server based on the cleaned up modulelist.txt</li>
	<li>Any moodle courses with a valid portico identifier in the shortname will have that put in the portico id field (the idnumber)</li>
	<li>Any moodle course with a valid portico identifer field that is NOT mapped - will have a 1-1 mapping created</li>
	<li>Spend a couple of hours testing both the admin interface - portico XML processing and automatic course creation</li>
</ul>


<p><strong>On Live</strong></p>
<ul>
	<li>Pete to set up a 'data cleaned' version of the SITS filter on the dev server based on the cleaned up modulelist.txt</li>
	<li>Any moodle courses with a valid portico identifier in the shortname will have that put in the portico id field (the idnumber)</li>
	<li>Any moodle course with a valid portico identifer field that is NOT mapped - will have a 1-1 mapping created</li>
</ul>


<h1>Test plan on dev (brief)</h1>

<p><strong>Basic stuff</strong></p>

<ul>
	<li>choose two mappings - a one to one and one to many</li>
	<li>empty both courses in Moodle</li>
	<li>run the process_xml code in the sitsfilter and then the IMS enterprise import in Moodle dev</li>
	<li>check that the correct people are enrolled</li>
</ul>


<p><strong>Course creation</strong></p>
<ul>
	<li>enable automatic course creation in Moodle DEV</li>
	<li>run the IMS enterprise enrolment in DEV</li>
</ul>


<p>Check a few created courses at random - they should all be non live</p>

<h2>On live ...</h2>

<ul>
	<li>turn off IMS enterprise enrolment (it's off)</li>
	<li>set up the sits filter with clean data as on dev (done)</li>
	<li>WAIT until 1 AUG - otherwise we get last years students enrolled!</li>
	<li>to start using the new sitsfilter - change the filename in the IMS enterprise settings - then run it</li>
	<li>suggest doing this at an at risk period the first time it is run and backing up the database first - just in case</li>
	<li>to revert back - simply change the name back to the old file (and export the modulelist.txt from the sits filter and put it in the usual place</li>
</ul>


<ul>
	<li>&nbsp;</li>
</ul>

21553218215599612<p>Hello Andrea,</p>

<p>Following your correspondence on Moodle over the last few days I wanted to respond to you with the current status on your queries and what we are doing to improve and develop the Moodle service at UCL.</p>

<p><strong>Problem in the exam on the afternoon of Fri 3rd Dec</strong></p>

<p>We've taken a close look at the access and error logs for the Moodle apache application servers and the Moodle database servers for that afternoon and can see no evidence of any problems.</p>

<p>A bit of background on how Moodle logs items. When a quiz is split over multiple pages, Moodle logs each new page as 'quiz continue attemp' (truncated like this)! whenever you move from page to page or click the 'save without submitting' button.</p>

<p>When finished, the candidate clicks the 'submit all and finish' button. A pop-up javascript prompt then asks - 'You are about to close this attempt. Once you close the attempt you will no longer be able to change your answers'.</p>

<p>If you click OK to submit - Moodle logs it as 'quiz close attempt'.</p>

<p>For the candidate concerned, Moodle's own logs show the quiz starting,  a gap of some fifteen minutes and then the quiz was closed. The apache logs concur.</p>

<p>The only explanation we can see is that the student clicked on the wrong button (and presumably the popup javascript warning too). In stressful situations mistakes are easily made.</p>

<p><span style="color: rgb(153,51,51);">We are aware you witnessed the student's problem first hand, however we feel there may have been some previous activity which caused the problem and the full extent of what actually happened was only witnessed by the individual. There aren't many technical solutions we can consider here - something like video cameras or screen monitoring software would be unworkable or very intrusive towards the student and the experience (especially during a stressful time).</span></p>

<p><span style="color: rgb(153,51,51);">If you are concerned about students losing their work then we suggest that if this happens again the student and invigilator are advised to leave the computer in the state it was in and to seek assistance from support staff immediately - who can then try to resolve the situation. Ideally the workstation needs to be examined and the server logs stored for analysis.</span></p>

<p><span style="color: rgb(153,51,51);">Students should be advised that if a problem occurs to instantly stop - completely - and ask for help - otherwise they may be subject to data loss. The very nature of web browsing and human behaviour does mean that sometimes things happen that are not simple to diagnose, particularly from the exam room itself.</span></p>

<p><strong>Response to any other queries Andrea has reported ...?</strong></p>
<ul>
	<li>...</li>
	<li>...</li>
	<li>...</li>
</ul>


<p>We do value your feedback and comments on Moodle and take any queries you have very seriously.&nbsp; If there are times when the Moodle servers/database/application appear to be causing problems we appreciate prompt reports on this and do try to respond as soon as possible to resolve any problems.&nbsp; As you point out the use of Moodle has increased greatly in the last year, and is going to increase even further; we are working to expand the capacity of the Moodle service to cope with the expected increase in load over the coming years.</p>

<p>Some improvements we have already made or are planned to be made in the coming months are:</p>
<ul>
	<li>Adjusting the Apache settings on the Moodle application servers to make them as efficient as possible (some of these changes were applied on Thursday morning, we will continue to monitor this and apply changes as necessary)</li>
	<li>Truncating and optimising the Moodle database regularly to keep it working as efficiently as possible</li>
	<li>Increasing the RAM in the application servers</li>
	<li>Tuning the database settings.&nbsp; We are investigating options including whether it may be prudent to change the database engine.</li>
	<li>Migrating the servers to new infrastructure which will allow better resilience and high availability</li>
	<li>Securing the storage and bandwidth needed for the increased numbers of users using Moodle in the coming years</li>
	<li>Increasing the number of application servers to cope with the anticipated load</li>
	<li>Improving server monitoring tools so that we are made aware of any potential problems and can begin to resolve them as soon as possible</li>
	<li>Moodle has been placed on the 'critical availability' list of ISD  services, where an ISD manager is contacted in the case of any problems</li>
	<li>taking expert advice from moodle.org on managing a large Moodle installation</li>
</ul>


<p>Please do keep in touch and report any comments you have with Moodle to the LTSS in the first instance so that we can track, monitor and respond to them.</p>21553547117106054<p>See SCPs 3900 and 4940</p>

<p>Most recent was 6th Jan 2011 on course 6093 - unable to view gradebook or quiz items. This was for a course that was reset. Odd.&nbsp;</p>

<p>The mdl_grade_items table should have one entry per course and then one entry for each gradeable item in that course. (The categoryid for these items should be the iteminstance of the course entry).</p>

<p>Confused? See the SQL query in the table below - this shows a malfunctioning course with two course entries.</p>

<p>If there are no gradeable items and just two course entries, to make it clear which is the 'correct' id as far as Moodle is concerned - just add a dummy assignment to the course - you can see below that 15515 is the correct item!</p>

<p>You can then zap the offending duplicate. In the case of course 6093 - there were no items in the mdl_grade_items table for the various quizzes - how this happened is a mystery.</p>

<p>The fix is to zap the duplicate course entry and then edit and save each quiz / assignment that's missing to create a new entry in the mdl_grade_items table.&nbsp;</p>

<p>Running the following query shows for this example that there are two items at 'course level' and the first one needs zapping.</p>

<ac:structured-macro ac:name="noformat"><ac:plain-text-body><!\[CDATA\[
mysql> select id, courseid, categoryid, itemtype, itemname, iteminstance from mdl_grade_items where courseid=6093;
+-------+----------+------------+----------+----------------------------------------------+--------------+
| id | courseid | categoryid | itemtype | itemname | iteminstance |
+-------+----------+------------+----------+----------------------------------------------+--------------+
| 45569 | 6093 | NULL | course | NULL | 15513 |
| 45855 | 6093 | 15515 | mod | dummy activity added by Pete - please ignore | 10395 |
| 45741 | 6093 | 15515 | mod | ARMS II assignment 1 | 3909 |
| 45743 | 6093 | 15515 | mod | Turn it in: Assignment 2 | 3911 |
| 45845 | 6093 | NULL | course | NULL | 15515 |
+-------+----------+------------+----------+----------------------------------------------+--------------+

5 rows in set (0.00 sec)

mysql> delete from mdl_grade_items where id=45569;
Query OK, 1 row affected (0.02 sec)
]] ></ac:plain-text-body></ac:structured-macro>21707336417109409<p><strong>Total Moodle at UCL</strong></p>

<h1>WordPress</h1>21776200417795034<h1>Turnitin - performance problems</h1>

<p>Tuesday 3rd May 2011 - around 00:18 - moodle b had severe problems! All down to a single user with Turnitin. Seems a little odd - abnormally high number of requests for the submission inbox over a short period (70 odd over 30 seconds).</p>

<p>total dbqueries - 3,614,447 (over the space of a few minutes)</p>


<p>this course <a href="http://moodle.ucl.ac.uk/course/view.php?id=10513">http://moodle.ucl.ac.uk/course/view.php?id=10513</a></p>






<p>this assignment - <a href="http://moodle.ucl.ac.uk/mod/turnitintool/view.php?id=399641">http://moodle.ucl.ac.uk/mod/turnitintool/view.php?id=399641</a></p>







<p>all from this IP address - 78.105.78.35</p>

<p>Later on Tuesday - Turnitin UK major outage (so not a problem at our end)!</p>

<h1>The big problem - the submission inbox</h1>


<p>Detailed analysis of Moodle shows that occasionally, there appears to be a MASSIVE amount of database activity. Sometimes over 100,000 db queries (from Moodle's own reliable performance stats).</p>


<p>This is turnitin.&nbsp; Occasionally the submission inbox does lots of extra SQL, then the page seemingly reloads.</p>


<p>The stats quoted for db queries below are a count of ALL moodle db queries - not just turnitin specific ones. eg - Moodle home page is around 76.</p>


<p><strong>See the three attached files for the sql and see the login SQL for comparison.</strong></p>

<p>In addition to the high number of queries coming all at once,&nbsp; some are potentially hard work - similar in fact to the slow queries during log in.</p>

<p>So - for an assignment with 50 submissions - it's a bit like that number logging in at once. Or possibly worse.</p>


<h4>Here's the apache error / Moodle perf stats (from my Mac)</h4>

<p>SELECT id, category, shortname, fullname, theme FROM mdl_course m where theme &lt;&gt; '' AND theme NOT LIKE '%ucl-new%' order by theme;</p>

<p>and users</p>


<p>SELECT id, username, firstname, lastname, theme, email FROM mdl_user m where theme &lt;&gt; '' AND theme NOT LIKE '%ucl-new%' order by theme;</p>

<p>To fix</p>

<p>UPDATE mdl_course  set theme='' where (theme &lt;&gt; '' AND theme NOT LIKE '%ucl-new%' );</p>

<p>UPDATE mdl_user set theme='' where (theme &lt;&gt; '' AND theme NOT LIKE '%ucl-new%' );<br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>21776437817797406<h2>Pros and Cons</h2>

21776611518415851<p>Things to try out</p>
<ul>
	<li>automatic 1 to 1 course creation for any new module found in Portico XML (for UCL depts)</li>
	<li>or report of all portico modules NOT mapped in any way (option to create them)?</li>
	<li>stats - no courses total enrolled</li>
</ul>


<p>Pete will demonstrate each of these steps - these are just reminder notes.</p>

<p>The sits filter testing is carried out away from live Moodle, you will therefore be provided with the following</p>
<ul>
	<li>a test Moodle instance</li>
	<li>a test UCL tools instance that matches</li>
	<li>up to date Portico XML in the right folder</li>
</ul>


<p>Initially you should concentrate on testing a single mapping at a time in some detail. To test a mapping, it's necessary to do the following</p>
<ul>
	<li>check in Portico to list the members of the modules included in the test</li>
	<li>check Pete has put the latest Portico XML in place for testing</li>
	<li>run scan_xml to process the Portico XML file</li>
	<li>in the sits filter - check the 'members' for each mapping under test (should match the Portico report)</li>
	<li>run the IMS enterprise import on the test Moodle instance and check the courses concerned</li>
	<li>try deleting users from the course and rerun scan_xml and the IMS enterprise import - the deleted users should be added in</li>
</ul>


<p>There are basically three mapping scenarios to test.</p>
<ol>
	<li>a simple one to one mapping of a Portico module to a course with matching identifer Portico codes, eg - INSTG001</li>
	<li>a one to one mapping of a Portico module to a course with non-matching codes, eg: INSTG001_submissions - a totally separate course</li>
	<li>a one to many mapping where one Moodle course has more than one Portico module assigned, eg BENG2009_BENGG017</li>
</ol>


<p>There are three methods of creating a new mapping to test</p>
<ol>
	<li>from searching for an existing Moodle course</li>
	<li>from searching for a Portico module</li>
	<li>a 'custom' new Moodle course&nbsp;</li>
</ol>


<p>Additional features</p>
<ul>
	<li>mapping diagnostics - this will show any duplicate portico identifiers in Moodle (these need fixing)</li>
	<li>automatic course creation (we may decide not to use this) - enable this in the IMS enterprise admin page on Moodle and check that courses are created</li>
</ul>


<p>Big test</p>
<ul>
	<li>ask Pete to dump the mappings and re-import the entire modulelist.txt file&nbsp;</li>
	<li>will need to fix any issues with errors / typos in the file if it goes wrong</li>
	<li>once it's imported correctly - run scan_xml and IMS enterprise import</li>
	<li>check some courses at random</li>
	<li>change a mapping for a course - run scan_xml and IMS enterprise import and check Moodle appears to match the mapping</li>
</ul>
21838311018416043<p>A user reported a strange corruption of their Moodle course page. <a href="http://moodle.ucl.ac.uk/course/view.php?id=12559">http://moodle.ucl.ac.uk/course/view.php?id=12559</a></p>









<p>See screenshots below (with and without editing on).</p>

<p>Basically the top section of the page appears to have a weird iframe in it with some sort of nonsense login links. There is no EDIT icon etc.</p>




<p><ac:image ac:border="true" ac:thumbnail="true"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Screen shot 2011-05-20 at 10.27.22.png" /></ac:image><br />
<ac:image ac:border="true" ac:thumbnail="true"><ri:attachment ri:filename="Screen shot 2011-05-20 at 10.27.36.png" /></ac:image></p>

<p>LTSS had looked into this - and if they can't fix it, it usually means trouble. Jess mentioned she wasn't entirely familiar with the moodle database. Me neither, so I thought this deserved a wiki&nbsp; page for future reference.</p>



<h4>step 1</h4>

<p>Backed up and restored the course to my mac - unfortunately the restore failed, so that kind of complicates things. (Locally I can display the SQL queries on screen with the page - very handy).</p>


<h4>step 2</h4>

<p>SELECT \* FROM mdl_course where id=12559</p>

<p>The stuff on the page is held in the modinfo field of the mdl_course table. This is a serialised array that looks like this&nbsp;</p>
<ac:macro ac:name="code"><ac:plain-text-body><![CDATA[
a:5:{i:501699;O:8:"stdClass":10:{s:2:"id";s:5:"27291";s:2:"cm";i:501699;s:3:"mod";s:5:"forum";s:7:"section";s:1:"0";s:7:"visible";s:1:"0";s:9:
]] ></ac:plain-text-body></ac:macro>
<p>and so on - you get the idea. Obviously this isn't terribly easy to read. I wrote a bit of PHP to extract it as below -&nbsp; note you have to escape all the double quotes for this to work.</p>

<ac:macro ac:name="code"><ac:plain-text-body><![CDATA[
$well_dodgy_string="a:5:{i:501699;O:8:\"stdClass\" etc (pasted in from the database field)

$array = unserialize($well_dodgy_string);
echo("<pre>");
print_r($array);
echo ("</pre>");
]] ></ac:plain-text-body></ac:macro>

<p>This gave the following</p>
<ac:macro ac:name="code"><ac:plain-text-body><![CDATA[

)

<p>All very interesting but doesn't seem to contain the rogue stuff.</p>


<p>I emptied the modinfo entry for the course in the database - no effect. Modinfo gets rebuilt if it's empty and the rebuilt entry was identical. So it wasn't that then. Worth a shot tho'.</p>

<p>Must be something odd in section zero.</p>


<h4>step 3</h4>

<p>Coffee I think</p>

<p>A Moodle course page contains modules and sections. Interestingly - none of the sections seem to have an EDIT icon against them on live Moodle (but do on pp and my local copy)</p>

<p>SELECT cm.\*, m.name as modname                             FROM mdl_modules m,                                  mdl_course_modules cm                             WHERE cm.course = 12559                             AND cm.module = m.id AND m.visible = 1</p>

<h4>step 4</h4>

<p>think outside the box</p>

<p>Someone's set the course to be LAMS format instead of topic based.</p>

<p>Solution - put it back like it was.</p>

]] ></ac:plain-text-body></ac:macro>21838435118418360<p>In times past it was 50/50 whether you went for myisam or innodb if you read the Moodle forums. However - now innodb is clearly the recommended way to go.</p>

<p>It makes sense therefore to start using innodb now.</p>

<h4>Miscellaneous database fixes</h4>

<p>The BIGINTS script needs running (requirement for Moodle 2 - might as well sort it now)</p>


<h4>Moodle archive</h4>

<p>This is an ideal platform to trial innodb. We can use innodb from the outset.</p>

<h4>Main Moodle service</h4>

<p>Based on lessons learned from the archive, the main Moodle service can be converted to innodb over the summer.</p>

<h4>Performance testing?</h4>

<p>It isn't possible to realistically test Moodle. However we can try some jmeter scripts on the dev server and compare myisam to innodb.</p>

<p>much much slower?</p>21838579118419452<h4>Departments in the Portico XML that don't have a proper matching category in Moodle yet</h4>

<p>It may indicate a typo in the Moodle category or that someone's changed it.</p>


<p>THE FOLLOWING 12 CATEGORY NAMES HAVE BEEN CHANGED IN MOODLE:</p>

<p>Based on actions from today's SIT meeting (18/07/2011) Jess updated 12 Moodle categories that means they will now map from the  SITS filter is we create any modules in them.</p>

<ul>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Institute of Archaeology &ndash; changed from &lsquo;Archaeology&rsquo;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Ear Institute &ndash; changed from &lsquo;UCL Ear Institute&rsquo;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Bartlett School of Construction &amp; Project Mngment &ndash; changed &ndash; abbreviated Management</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Centre for Advanced Spatial Analysis &ndash; changed - removed (CASA) from end</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Division of Infection and Immunity- changed &amp;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Civil, Environmental and Geomatic Engineering &ndash; changed &amp;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Centre for the Advancement of Learning &amp; Teaching &ndash; changed &ndash; removed (CALT) from end</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; English Language and Literature &ndash; changed &amp;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Science and Technology Studies &ndash; changed &amp;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Information Studies &ndash; changed - from &lsquo;Department of Information Students (formerly SLAIS)&rsquo;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;SSEES - School of Slavonic &amp; East European Studies &ndash; changed from &lsquo;UCL School of Slavonic and East European Studies&rsquo;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; School of Energy and Resources (Australia) &ndash; changed from &lsquo;School of Energy and Resources (SERAus)&rsquo;</li>
</ul>


<p>DIDN&rsquo;T CHANGE THESE:</p>

<p>A couple of these  non-changed ones may be able to be changed once the  restructuring is  finalised (see the 2 at the bottom of this email).</p>
<ul>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Division of Medical Education &ndash; not changed NOT THE SAME AS &lsquo;Academic Centre for Medical Education&rsquo;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Arts and Humanities Faculty Office &ndash; not changed &ndash; currently &lsquo;Arts and Humanities&rsquo;</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Development Planning Unit &ndash; NOT changed still &lsquo;Bartlett Development Planning Unit&rsquo; as all others proceeded by Bartlett</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Division of Population Health &ndash; can&rsquo;t find any Moodle courses only one in Biomedical Sciences / Epidemiology and Public Health</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Cancer Institute &ndash; can&rsquo;t find any modules &ndash; only biomedical MBBS, biosciences, Immunology and Molecular Pathology and bioc courses</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Division of Medicine &ndash; don&rsquo;t know if this is the same as Biomedical Sciences / Medicine so left alone.</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Centre for Maths &amp;Phys In Life Sci &amp;Exprmntal Biol &ndash; no way am I changed it to this. Doesn&rsquo;t make sense</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; European Social and Political Studies Office &ndash; can&rsquo;t find anything in Moodle to do with this</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Wellcome Trust Centre for the History of Medicine &ndash; not changed &ndash; can&rsquo;t find - only a few courses in Life Sciences / Division of Biosciences</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Natural Sciences &ndash; no category &ndash; can just find some courses in Life Sciences</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; UCL Medical School &ndash; not found &ndash; only found Biomedical Sciences / MBBS</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Political Science &ndash; not found</li>
	<li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; SSEES - East European Languages and Culture &ndash; not found (under category below maybe?)</li>

<p><strong>Notes from Pete</strong></p>

<p>SQL for empty portico id poseur - we can use the list of valid Portico modules to make sure we're not putting daft data into the portico id field in Moodle (strictly speaking the idnumber)</p>


<p>to see the scale of the problem</p>


<p>SELECT \*<br />
FROM <em>moodledbname</em>.mdl_course m<br />
WHERE length(m.shortname)=8<br />
AND length(m.idnumber)=0<br />
AND m.shortname in (select sits_code from <em>moodle_sits_managementdbname</em>.module)</p>

<p>to fix it</p>

<p>UPDATE <em>moodledbname</em>.mdl_course m</p>

<p>SET m.idnumber=m.shortname</p>

<p>WHERE length(m.shortname)=8<br />
AND length(m.idnumber)=0<br />
AND m.shortname in (select sits_code from <em>moodle_sits_managementdbname</em>.module)</p>21838827818421589<p>Current, test set up:</p>

<ul>
	<li>web server : <a href="http://moodlevm-a.ucl.ac.uk">moodlevm-a </a></li>
	<li>database server : moodlevm-db</li>
	<li>file server : moodle-nfs (mounted to /moodlefs/moodle), a complete copy of the file system taken overnight on thr 16th July.</li>
</ul>




<p>Differences from standard set up :</p>

<ul>
	<li>apache logs in /var/log/httpd</li>
	<li>db user : moodlevm_user / IlgcZMAK&pound;8</li>
	<li>Vivek has updated these Db engine to be InnoDB.</li>
</ul>



<p>This set up is due to be trashed once testing is complete.</p>

<p>moodlevm-b and moodlevm-c are also available, but are not used at present.</p>

<p>27th July : testing of database carried out.</p>

<p>We ran three Jmeter tests simultaneously</p>
<ul>
	<li>Login, search, Logout : 500 users</li>
	<li>Loading a stats page from the UCL tools : ucl_tools/mdl_log-stats.php</li>
	<li>Random deletion of a single entry from the mdl_log table : 1 deletion every 10 seconds.</li>
</ul>


<p>Results as described in email by Vivkek:</p>

<blockquote>
<p><br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<p>moodlevm:</p>

<p>----------------</p>

<p>Upto 500 select statements running simultaneously we have average 135 ms response times.</p>

<p>One a couple of delete statements on mdl_log running to delete random records along with the 500 select statements, the average response times are around 25 seconds with the peak being around 70 secs. I have hardly seen any I/O come waits on the machine with a maximum wait of around 5% for a 10 minute period.
<br class="atl-forced-newline" />
<br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<p>moodle-pp</p>

<p>----------------</p>

<p>On 500 connections being initiated from moodle-pp, the machine almost instantaneously came to a grinding halt with me not being able to run even basic commands. I requested Chris to stop the tests immediately otherwise the machine would have crashed but apart from the mysql thread utilizing the memory there were a whole host of http thread that were invoked as a result of the 500+ connection request which jammed the machine.
<br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<p>So all in all it seems that moodlevm is handling requests quite well even the highest level of simulated load that we have currently seen via moodle when we have had a maximum of 500 students logging in simultaneously. Even with deletes running alongside the selects the response times were still acceptable considering the fact the there were no indexes being used when deleting rows from the mdl_log table.
<br class="atl-forced-newline" />
<br class="atl-forced-newline" /></p>

<p>Conclusion</p>

<p>-----------------</p>

<p>I do see this as quite a good test considering the amount of load that we were able to simulate.</p>



<p>We do not have comparable stats with MySQL 5.0 but the considering that 5.0 does not have many of the features which MySQL 5.5 has and which helped manage the load on moodlevm, I would be rather skeptical of getting any better results from 5.0 on this load</p></blockquote>21838921618421628<h1>UCL Go!</h1>
